<p>The <b>Union of South American Nations</b> (<b>USAN</b>; Spanish: <i lang="es">Unión de Naciones Suramericanas</i>, <b>UNASUR</b>; Portuguese: <i lang="pt">União de Nações Sul-Americanas</i>, <b>UNASUL</b>; Dutch: <i lang="nl">Unie van Zuid-Amerikaanse Naties</i>, <b>UZAN</b>; and sometimes referred to as the <b>South American Union</b>) is an <a href="/wiki/Intergovernmentalism" title="Intergovernmentalism">intergovernmental</a> <a href="/wiki/Regional_organization" title="Regional organization">regional organization</a> that once comprised twelve South American countries; as of 2019, most have withdrawn.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/UNASUR_Constitutive_Treaty" title="UNASUR Constitutive Treaty">UNASUR Constitutive Treaty</a> was signed on 23 May 2008, at the Third Summit of Heads of State, held in <a href="/wiki/Bras%C3%ADlia" title="Brasília">Brasília</a>, Brazil.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc2_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc2-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> According to the Constitutive Treaty, the Union's headquarters will be located in <a href="/wiki/Quito" title="Quito">Quito</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ecuador" title="Ecuador">Ecuador</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bloomberg1_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bloomberg1-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> On 1 December 2010, Uruguay became the ninth state to ratify the UNASUR treaty, thus giving the union full legality.<sup id="cite_ref-buenosairesherald1_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-buenosairesherald1-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MercoPress2_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MercoPress2-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> As the Constitutive Treaty entered into force on 11 March 2011, UNASUR became a legal entity during a meeting of Foreign Ministers in <a href="/wiki/Ciudad_Mitad_del_Mundo" title="Ciudad Mitad del Mundo">Mitad del Mundo</a>, Ecuador, where they had laid the foundation stone for the Secretariat Headquarters.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>In April 2018, six countries—Argentina, Brazil, Chile, Colombia, Paraguay and Peru<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>—suspended their membership, and in August of the same year, Colombia announced its withdrawal from the organization.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>  In March 2019, Brazil's president <a href="/wiki/Jair_Bolsonaro" title="Jair Bolsonaro">Jair Bolsonaro</a> announced his country's intention to withdraw from the organization.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> On March 13, 2019, <a href="/wiki/Ecuador" title="Ecuador">Ecuador</a> announced that it will withdraw from the organization. The president of the country, <a href="/wiki/Lenin_Moreno" class="mw-redirect" title="Lenin Moreno">Lenin Moreno</a>, also asked the bloc to return the headquarters building of the organization, based in <a href="/wiki/Quito" title="Quito">Quito</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In January 2019, amid growing concern about Venezuela's <a href="/wiki/Nicolas_Maduro" class="mw-redirect" title="Nicolas Maduro">Nicolas Maduro</a>, a new group, <a href="/wiki/Forum_for_the_Progress_and_Development_of_South_America" title="Forum for the Progress and Development of South America">PROSUR</a>, has been advanced to "counteract the influence of what countries in the region call a dictatorship in Venezuela".<sup id="cite_ref-CreatingBloc_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CreatingBloc-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>  A Chilean summit to organize Prosur was held on 22 March 2019, and excluded Venezuela. Argentina, Brazil, Bolivia, Colombia, Chile, Ecuador, Uruguay, Paraguay, Peru, Guyana and Suriname were invited to join the new regional bloc.<sup id="cite_ref-ConfirmaCumbre_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ConfirmaCumbre-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Overview">Overview</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Union_of_South_American_Nations&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Overview">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>At the <a href="/wiki/2004_South_American_Summit" title="2004 South American Summit">Third South American Summit</a> on 8 December 2004, presidents or representatives from 12 South American nations signed the <i><a href="/wiki/Cusco_Declaration" title="Cusco Declaration">Cusco Declaration</a></i>, a two-page statement of intent announcing the foundation of the South American Community. Panama and Mexico attended the signing ceremony as observers in Brazil.
</p><p>The mechanics of the new entity came out of the First South American Community of Nations Heads of State Summit, which was held in Brasília on 29–30 September 2005. An important operating condition of UNASUR is that no new institutions will be created in the first phase, so as not to increase <a href="/wiki/Bureaucracy" title="Bureaucracy">bureaucracy</a>, and the community will use the existing institutions belonging to the previous <a href="/wiki/Trade_blocs" class="mw-redirect" title="Trade blocs">trade blocs</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Union_of_South_American_Nations&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Background">Background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Union_of_South_American_Nations&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="box-More_citations_needed plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Union_of_South_American_Nations&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Latin_American_integration" title="Latin American integration">Latin American integration</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Pan-Americanism" title="Pan-Americanism">Pan-Americanism</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Presidentes_de_pa%C3%ADses_da_Am%C3%A9rica_do_Sul_durante_a_primeira_reuni%C3%A3o_do_CASA_(4).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Presidentes_de_pa%C3%ADses_da_Am%C3%A9rica_do_Sul_durante_a_primeira_reuni%C3%A3o_do_CASA_%284%29.jpg/220px-Presidentes_de_pa%C3%ADses_da_Am%C3%A9rica_do_Sul_durante_a_primeira_reuni%C3%A3o_do_CASA_%284%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Presidentes_de_pa%C3%ADses_da_Am%C3%A9rica_do_Sul_durante_a_primeira_reuni%C3%A3o_do_CASA_%284%29.jpg/330px-Presidentes_de_pa%C3%ADses_da_Am%C3%A9rica_do_Sul_durante_a_primeira_reuni%C3%A3o_do_CASA_%284%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Presidentes_de_pa%C3%ADses_da_Am%C3%A9rica_do_Sul_durante_a_primeira_reuni%C3%A3o_do_CASA_%284%29.jpg/440px-Presidentes_de_pa%C3%ADses_da_Am%C3%A9rica_do_Sul_durante_a_primeira_reuni%C3%A3o_do_CASA_%284%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1967" data-file-height="1311" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Presidentes_de_pa%C3%ADses_da_Am%C3%A9rica_do_Sul_durante_a_primeira_reuni%C3%A3o_do_CASA_(4).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Heads of State of the then South American Community of Nations in <a href="/wiki/Brasilia" class="mw-redirect" title="Brasilia">Brasilia</a> in September 2005.</div></div></div>
<p>Between the 15th and 19th centuries, the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="Spanish colonization of the Americas">Spanish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="Portuguese colonization of the Americas">Portuguese</a> colonization brought about the establishment and development of <a href="/wiki/Colonial_empire" title="Colonial empire">colonial empires</a> in the Americas that integrated politically, economically and culturally vast extensions of the continent each with their respective metropolis.
</p><p>Since the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_American_wars_of_independence" title="Spanish American wars of independence">Spanish American wars of independence</a> a trend towards the political integration of the newly born republics of <a href="/wiki/Hispanic_America" title="Hispanic America">Hispanic America</a> became strong in the thinking of several independence leaders, influenced in turn by the <a href="/wiki/Enlightenment_in_Spain" title="Enlightenment in Spain">Spanish Enlightenment</a> and the <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution" title="French Revolution">French</a> and <a href="/wiki/American_Revolution" title="American Revolution">American</a> revolutions. A notable early exponent of this trend was <a href="/wiki/Francisco_de_Miranda" title="Francisco de Miranda">Francisco de Miranda</a>, who envisioned a federated republic encompassing all of Hispanic America, which he called "Colombia".
</p><p>The independence war efforts saw the concurrence of integrated armies composed by Spanish Americans of diverse regions on both sides of the conflict (v.g. Patriots and <a href="/wiki/Royalist_(Spanish_American_Revolution)" class="mw-redirect" title="Royalist (Spanish American Revolution)">Royalists</a>), and fighting all over the territories of many future nations. For example, the <a href="/wiki/Army_of_the_Andes" title="Army of the Andes">Army of the Andes</a> which was gathered in the <a href="/wiki/United_Provinces_of_the_River_Plate" class="mw-redirect" title="United Provinces of the River Plate">United Provinces of the River Plate</a> fought in <a href="/wiki/Chilean_War_of_Independence" title="Chilean War of Independence">Chile</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peruvian_War_of_Independence" title="Peruvian War of Independence">Peru</a> and Ecuador, and later integrated with <a href="/wiki/Military_career_of_Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar" title="Military career of Simón Bolívar">Simón Bolívar's Army</a> (which itself included troops of future Venezuela, Colombia and Ecuador) to further fight in Peru and the <a href="/wiki/Upper_Peru" title="Upper Peru">Upper Peru</a>.
</p><p>By the 1820s, the main proponent of a federation of the newly born republics was <a href="/wiki/Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar" title="Simón Bolívar">Simón Bolívar</a>, although this idea was shared by many notable contemporaries, including <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_de_San_Mart%C3%ADn" title="José de San Martín">José de San Martín</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bernardo_de_Monteagudo" title="Bernardo de Monteagudo">Bernardo de Monteagudo</a>, under either republican or constitutional monarchical governments. In 1826, Bolívar summoned a conference to be held in Panama, which was to be known as the <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Panama" title="Congress of Panama">"Amphictyonic" Congress of Panama</a> because of the parallelism with the Hellenic <a href="/wiki/Amphictyonic_League" title="Amphictyonic League">Amphictyonic League</a>. The Congress was attended by <a href="/wiki/Gran_Colombia" title="Gran Colombia">Gran Colombia</a> (including present-day Colombia, Venezuela, Panama and Ecuador), the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Republic_of_Central_America" title="Federal Republic of Central America">Federal Republic of Central America</a> (including present-day Costa Rica, Nicaragua, El Salvador, Honduras and Guatemala), the <a href="/wiki/United_Mexican_States_(1824%E2%80%931864)" class="mw-redirect" title="United Mexican States (1824–1864)">United Mexican States</a>, and Peru. The ostensible intention was to form a defensive league that could prevent foreign expansionism and foster the interests of the Spanish American republics. The Congress' conclusions, however, were not ratified by the participants, except for Gran Colombia. Soon after, both Gran Colombia and the United Provinces of Central America fell apart and the whole of Hispanic America was <a href="/wiki/Balkanization" title="Balkanization">balkanized</a> by competing national governments.
</p><p>By the 1990s, however, Brazil had consolidated as the most powerful country in South America (accounting for half of the regional GDP) and began to promote the notion of a united South America (a new regional framing) where Brasilia would be pivotal. The project did not take hold until the United States' foreign policy priorities turned to other regions in the 2000s.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Formation">Formation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Union_of_South_American_Nations&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Formation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cusco_Declaration" title="Cusco Declaration">Cusco Declaration</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Unasul_12.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Unasul_12.jpg/220px-Unasul_12.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Unasul_12.jpg/330px-Unasul_12.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Unasul_12.jpg/440px-Unasul_12.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2480" data-file-height="1772" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Unasul_12.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>South American presidents gathered during an extraordinary meeting for the signing of the <a href="/wiki/UNASUR_Constitutive_Treaty" title="UNASUR Constitutive Treaty">UNASUR Constitutive Treaty</a> in May 2008 in Brasilia.</div></div></div>
<p>The complete integration between the Andean Community and the <a href="/wiki/Mercosur" title="Mercosur">Mercosur</a> nations was formalized during the meeting of South American heads of state that took place on 23 May 2008 in <a href="/wiki/Bras%C3%ADlia" title="Brasília">Brasília</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/2004_South_American_Summit" title="2004 South American Summit">2004 South American Summit</a>, representatives of twelve South American nations signed the <a href="/wiki/Cuzco_Declaration" class="mw-redirect" title="Cuzco Declaration">Cuzco Declaration</a>, a two-page letter of intent announcing the establishment of the then-named "South American Community of Nations". Panama and Mexico were present as observers. The leaders announced the intention of modeling the new community in the mold of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>, including a unified passport, a parliament and, eventually, a single currency. The then Secretary General of the Andean Community <a href="/wiki/Allan_Wagner" class="mw-redirect" title="Allan Wagner">Allan Wagner</a> speculated that an advanced union such as the EU should be possible within the next fifteen years.
</p><p>After Argentina, Bolivia, Chile, Ecuador, Guyana, Peru, Suriname and Venezuela, Uruguay became the ninth nation to ratify the constitutive treaty of the organization on 1 December 2010, thus completing the minimum number of ratifications Necessary for the entry into force of the Treaty, on 11 March 2011<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-buenosairesherald1_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-buenosairesherald1-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MercoPress2_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MercoPress2-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> With the entry into force of the Treaty,<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> UNASUR became a legal entity during the Summit Ministers of Foreign Affairs, in <a href="/wiki/Ciudad_Mitad_del_Mundo" title="Ciudad Mitad del Mundo">Mitad del Mundo</a>, Ecuador, where the cornerstone was laid for the headquarters of the General Secretariat of the Union.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Naming">Naming</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Union_of_South_American_Nations&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Naming">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kirchner-UN_General_Assembly_(2007).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Kirchner-UN_General_Assembly_%282007%29.jpg/220px-Kirchner-UN_General_Assembly_%282007%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="166" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Kirchner-UN_General_Assembly_%282007%29.jpg/330px-Kirchner-UN_General_Assembly_%282007%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Kirchner-UN_General_Assembly_%282007%29.jpg/440px-Kirchner-UN_General_Assembly_%282007%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1776" data-file-height="1339" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kirchner-UN_General_Assembly_(2007).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/N%C3%A9stor_Kirchner" title="Néstor Kirchner">Néstor Kirchner</a>, first Secretary General of UNASUR</div></div></div>
<p>On 28 December 2005, Chilean former foreign minister Ignacio Walker proposed that the Union's former designation, the <b>South American Community of Nations</b>, abbreviated as <b>CSN</b>, be changed to <i>South American Union</i>; nevertheless, many members responded that that proposal had already been rejected to prevent confusion since its acronym of U.S.A. (Spanish: <i>Unión Sudamericana</i>) would be easily confused for the United States of America. In the press, the phrase "United States of South America" was bandied about as an <a href="/wiki/Analogy" title="Analogy">analogy</a> to the United States to reflect the economic and political power that the union would have on the world stage.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The name was finally changed on 16 April 2007 to <i>Union of South American Nations</i>. The new name was jointly agreed by all member states during the first day of meeting at the First <a href="/wiki/South_American_Energy_Summit" title="South American Energy Summit">South American Energy Summit</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-terra1_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-terra1-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> held at <a href="/wiki/Isla_Margarita" class="mw-redirect" title="Isla Margarita">Isla Margarita</a>, Venezuela.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Leadership_crisis">Leadership crisis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Union_of_South_American_Nations&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Leadership crisis">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>After Colombian Ernesto Samper completed his term as Secretary General in January 2017, the UNASUR governments have been unable to reach consensus on the organization's future leadership.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Venezuela, with the support of Bolivia and Suriname, has blocked the nomination of Argentine diplomat José Octavio Bordón.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In August 2017, six members of UNASUR—Argentina, Brazil, Chile, Colombia, Paraguay and Peru—joined in forming the <a href="/wiki/Lima_Group" title="Lima Group">Lima Group</a>, a coalition of Western Hemisphere nations that repudiates the Venezuela government of Nicolás Maduro as antidemocratic.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> In February 2018, Maduro was disinvited from the <a href="/wiki/8th_Summit_of_the_Americas" title="8th Summit of the Americas">Summit of the Americas</a> hosted by Peru (held in Lima in April 2018). In response, Bolivia's leftist president <a href="/wiki/Evo_Morales" title="Evo Morales">Evo Morales</a> urged Unasur to defend Venezuela, stating "Unasur should call an emergency meeting and enforce the sovereignty of a brotherly people."<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Morales acceded to the rotating role of president <a href="/wiki/Pro_tempore" title="Pro tempore">pro tempore</a> of UNASUR on 17 April 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 20 April 2018, six countries—Argentina, Brazil, Chile, Colombia, Paraguay and Peru—announced that they would suspend their own membership for a year until the regional group became more organized.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Chilean Foreign Minister Roberto Ampuero stated that the organization "isn't getting anywhere, there is no integration" and that "We can't be throwing this money to an institution that doesn't work."<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> A briefing sent to the Brazilian cabinet stated that the countries share the view that Bolivia's leadership of the block has been ineffective.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> Paraguayan Foreign Minister stated that his country's objection concerned the failure to put a new Secretary General in place, and the need to make the organization less ideological, but did not reflect negatively on Bolivia's leadership.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>  Bolivian Foreign Minister Fernando Huanacuni called an emergency meeting for May 2018 to attempt to resolve the crisis.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Countries_renouncing_the_treaty">Countries renouncing the treaty</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Union_of_South_American_Nations&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Countries renouncing the treaty">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Colombia">Colombia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Union_of_South_American_Nations&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Colombia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>On 28 August 2018, Colombian president <a href="/wiki/Iv%C3%A1n_Duque" class="mw-redirect" title="Iván Duque">Iván Duque</a> announced that foreign minister <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Holmes_Trujillo" title="Carlos Holmes Trujillo">Carlos Holmes</a> had officially notified Unasur of their intention to leave the bloc within the next 6 months, denouncing it as an institution created by Hugo Chávez to sideline existing international treaties and referring to it as an accomplice to what they referred to as the <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Venezuela" title="Human rights in Venezuela">dictatorship in Venezuela</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Brazil">Brazil</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Union_of_South_American_Nations&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Brazil">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>On 7 March 2019 Brazilian president <a href="/wiki/Jair_Bolsonaro" title="Jair Bolsonaro">Jair Bolsonaro</a> announced that Brazil would withdraw from Unasur and join the newly created <a href="/wiki/Forum_for_the_Progress_and_Development_of_South_America" title="Forum for the Progress and Development of South America">Prosur</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Ecuador">Ecuador</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Union_of_South_American_Nations&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Ecuador">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>On 13 March 2019 Ecuadorian president Lenin Moreno announced that Ecuador would withdraw from Unasur and join the newly created <a href="/wiki/Forum_for_the_Progress_and_Development_of_South_America" title="Forum for the Progress and Development of South America">Prosur</a>. Moreno also asked the bloc to return the headquarters building of the organization, based in <a href="/wiki/Quito" title="Quito">Quito</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Structure">Structure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Union_of_South_American_Nations&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Structure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="box-Update plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Update" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><img alt="Ambox current red.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/42px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png" decoding="async" width="42" height="34" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/63px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/84px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="360" data-file-height="290" /></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section's <b><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Accuracy_dispute" title="Wikipedia:Accuracy dispute">factual accuracy</a> may be compromised due to out-of-date information</b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please update this article to reflect recent events or newly available information.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">March 2019</span>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:UNASUR_(Ecuador).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/UNASUR_%28Ecuador%29.jpg/220px-UNASUR_%28Ecuador%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/UNASUR_%28Ecuador%29.jpg/330px-UNASUR_%28Ecuador%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/UNASUR_%28Ecuador%29.jpg/440px-UNASUR_%28Ecuador%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4608" data-file-height="2592" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:UNASUR_(Ecuador).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Former headquarters of UNASUR</div></div></div>
<p>The presidents of each member nation had an annual meeting, which was the top political mandate. The first meeting was held in <a href="/wiki/Brasilia" class="mw-redirect" title="Brasilia">Brasilia</a> on 29 and 30 September 2005. The second meeting was held in <a href="/wiki/Cochabamba" title="Cochabamba">Cochabamba</a>, Bolivia, on 8 and 9 December 2006. The third meeting was held in Brasília – this meeting should have taken place in Cartagena (Colombia), but was postponed because of tension between Ecuador, Colombia and Venezuela. It was at this meeting that UNASUR was formalized and in which the <a href="/wiki/UNASUR_Constitutive_Treaty" title="UNASUR Constitutive Treaty">Constitutive Treaty</a> of the organization was signed.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The foreign ministers of each country met once every six months. They made concrete proposals for action and executive decision. The Permanent Representative Committee of the President of <a href="/wiki/Mercosur" title="Mercosur">Mercosur</a> and the Director of the Mercosur Department, the Secretary General of the <a href="/wiki/Andean_Community" title="Andean Community">Andean Community</a>, the Secretary General of <a href="/wiki/ALADI" class="mw-redirect" title="ALADI">ALADI</a> and the Permanent Secretaries of any institution for regional cooperation and integration, <a href="/wiki/Amazon_Cooperation_Treaty_Organization" title="Amazon Cooperation Treaty Organization">Amazon Cooperation Treaty Organization</a>, among others, also attended these meetings.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>On 9 December 2005, the Strategic Reflection Commission on the South American Integration Process was created. It consists of 12 members, whose function is to elaborate proposals that will help in the process of integration among the South American nations. These proposals were to be made at the 2nd UNASUR Meeting (2006).<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/South_American_Parliament" title="South American Parliament">South American Parliament</a> was located in <a href="/wiki/Cochabamba" title="Cochabamba">Cochabamba</a>, Bolivia, while the headquarters of its bank, the <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_the_South" title="Bank of the South">Bank of the South</a> was located in <a href="/wiki/Caracas" title="Caracas">Caracas</a>, Venezuela.<sup id="cite_ref-bloomberg1_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bloomberg1-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Executive Committee, created at the 2nd UNASUR Meeting, was transformed into the Political Commission or Council of Deputies, in accordance with the Decisions of the Political Dialogue. The text prepared by heads of state to form UNASUR was approved at the 3rd UNASUR Meeting in Brasília on 23 May 2008. This meeting was scheduled to take place in Cartagena de Indias, Colombia, on 24–28 January 2008, but was postponed because of tensions between Ecuador, Colombia and Venezuela.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Secretary_General">Secretary General</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Union_of_South_American_Nations&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Secretary General">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Secretary_General_of_the_Union_of_South_American_Nations" title="Secretary General of the Union of South American Nations">Secretary General of the Union of South American Nations</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ernesto_Samper_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Ernesto_Samper_%28cropped%29.jpg/170px-Ernesto_Samper_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="232" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Ernesto_Samper_%28cropped%29.jpg/255px-Ernesto_Samper_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Ernesto_Samper_%28cropped%29.jpg/340px-Ernesto_Samper_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="851" data-file-height="1162" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ernesto_Samper_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Ernesto_Samper" title="Ernesto Samper">Ernesto Samper</a>, the most recent <a href="/wiki/Secretary_General_of_the_Union_of_South_American_Nations" title="Secretary General of the Union of South American Nations">Secretary General</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>A Secretary General is the legal representative of the Secretariat in <a href="/wiki/Quito" title="Quito">Quito</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ecuador" title="Ecuador">Ecuador</a>. Former Ecuadorian president <a href="/wiki/Rodrigo_Borja" class="mw-redirect" title="Rodrigo Borja">Rodrigo Borja</a> was nominated to this position but resigned a few days before the formation of the USAN in May 2008. On 4 May, <a href="/wiki/N%C3%A9stor_Kirchner" title="Néstor Kirchner">Néstor Kirchner</a> of Argentina was appointed as the first Secretary General, despite resistance from Colombia, Uruguay, and Peru. After the death of Néstor Kirchner in 2010, there was a period of time when the position went unfilled, which eventually ended when <a href="/wiki/Mar%C3%ADa_Emma_Mej%C3%ADa_V%C3%A9lez" title="María Emma Mejía Vélez">María Emma Mejía Vélez</a> was elected in March 2011. After Ernesto Samper completed his term in January 2017, UNASUR members have been unable to come to consensus on a successor.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Presidency_pro_tempore">Presidency pro tempore</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Union_of_South_American_Nations&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Presidency pro tempore">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/President_pro_tempore_of_the_Union_of_South_American_Nations" title="President pro tempore of the Union of South American Nations">President pro tempore of the Union of South American Nations</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Evo_Morales_2011.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Evo_Morales_2011.jpg/170px-Evo_Morales_2011.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Evo_Morales_2011.jpg/255px-Evo_Morales_2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Evo_Morales_2011.jpg/340px-Evo_Morales_2011.jpg 2x" data-file-width="936" data-file-height="1248" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Evo_Morales_2011.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Evo_Morales" title="Evo Morales">Evo Morales</a> was the most recent <a href="/wiki/President_pro_tempore_of_the_Union_of_South_American_Nations" title="President pro tempore of the Union of South American Nations">President of UNASUR</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>The temporary presidency will be governed by a year and will be rotating among the member countries between each UNASUR meeting. According to the document "Decisions of the Political Dialogue", which was signed during the 1st South American Energy Meeting, a permanent general cabinet will be created and headquartered in <a href="/wiki/Quito" title="Quito">Quito</a>, Ecuador.<sup id="cite_ref-Secretary-General2_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Secretary-General2-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Councils_and_bodies">Councils and bodies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Union_of_South_American_Nations&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Councils and bodies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Council_of_Economy_and_Finance">Council of Economy and Finance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Union_of_South_American_Nations&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Council of Economy and Finance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:UNASUR,_Reuni%C3%B3n_Ordinaria_del_Consejo_de_Ministro_de_Relaciones_Exteriores_(9623068687).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/UNASUR%2C_Reuni%C3%B3n_Ordinaria_del_Consejo_de_Ministro_de_Relaciones_Exteriores_%289623068687%29.jpg/220px-UNASUR%2C_Reuni%C3%B3n_Ordinaria_del_Consejo_de_Ministro_de_Relaciones_Exteriores_%289623068687%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/UNASUR%2C_Reuni%C3%B3n_Ordinaria_del_Consejo_de_Ministro_de_Relaciones_Exteriores_%289623068687%29.jpg/330px-UNASUR%2C_Reuni%C3%B3n_Ordinaria_del_Consejo_de_Ministro_de_Relaciones_Exteriores_%289623068687%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/UNASUR%2C_Reuni%C3%B3n_Ordinaria_del_Consejo_de_Ministro_de_Relaciones_Exteriores_%289623068687%29.jpg/440px-UNASUR%2C_Reuni%C3%B3n_Ordinaria_del_Consejo_de_Ministro_de_Relaciones_Exteriores_%289623068687%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4774" data-file-height="3183" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:UNASUR,_Reuni%C3%B3n_Ordinaria_del_Consejo_de_Ministro_de_Relaciones_Exteriores_(9623068687).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Meeting of Ministers of Foreign Affairs of the members of Unasur.</div></div></div>
<p>The Economic and Financial Council of Unasur was established on 12 August 2011, in <a href="/wiki/Buenos_Aires" title="Buenos Aires">Buenos Aires</a>, during a meeting of Finance Ministers and representatives of the Central Banks of the twelve countries of the region. Argentine Deputy Economy Minister Roberto Feletti said that the Council would study measures to strengthen regional trade in national currencies without the use of dollar. "We have reached an agreement on three axes of work and one of them is to move forward with multilateral payment mechanisms, to sustain trade and protect the volumes of reserves," Feletti said, noting that trade between countries in the region moves 120&#160;billion dollars Yearly. "The use of national currencies, excluding the dollar, protects reserves and increases trade because there are lower transaction rates." He also detailed plans of the technical groups focused on the development and strengthening of Development Banks, such as the Andean Development Corporation (CAF) and the <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_the_South" title="Bank of the South">Bank of the South</a>. He explained that the technicians will review the Latin American Reserve Fund (FLAR), aiming at in order to give greater capacity to intervene to the governments of the bloc in case of speculative attacks against currency or <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_debt" class="mw-redirect" title="Sovereign debt">sovereign debt</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Council_of_South_American_Defense">Council of South American Defense</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Union_of_South_American_Nations&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Council of South American Defense">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Council_of_South_American_Defense" title="Council of South American Defense">Council of South American Defense</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bandeiras_UNASUL.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Bandeiras_UNASUL.jpg/220px-Bandeiras_UNASUL.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Bandeiras_UNASUL.jpg/330px-Bandeiras_UNASUL.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Bandeiras_UNASUL.jpg/440px-Bandeiras_UNASUL.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1333" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bandeiras_UNASUL.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Flags of the member countries of UNASUR in front of the headquarters of the organization, in Ecuador.</div></div></div>
<p>The creation of a <a href="/wiki/Council_of_South_American_Defense" title="Council of South American Defense">Council of South American Defense</a> was proposed by Brazil and discussed for the first time at a summit of the South American presidents in April 2008. The project was extensively discussed throughout 2008. The then Brazilian Defense Minister, Nelson Jobim, said in April 2008 that the Council would be formed after the "political" decision of the presidents who participated in the launch of the Union of South American Nations (UNASUR) on 23 May 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-G1_2008_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-G1_2008-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 15 December 2008, at the extraordinary UNASUR summit, the creation of the South American Defense Council was finally approved. The defense ministers of Argentina, Brazil, Uruguay, Paraguay, Bolivia, Colombia, Ecuador, Peru, Chile, Guyana, Suriname and Venezuela. The Defense Council is responsible for developing joint defense policies, promoting the exchange of personnel among the Armed Forces of each country, conducting joint military exercises, participating in United Nations peace operations, promoting the exchange of analyzes on the world defense scenarios and the integration of industrial bases of military equipment.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="South_American_Council_of_Health">South American Council of Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Union_of_South_American_Nations&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: South American Council of Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="box-Update plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Update" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><img alt="Ambox current red.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/42px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png" decoding="async" width="42" height="34" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/63px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/84px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="360" data-file-height="290" /></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section's <b><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Accuracy_dispute" title="Wikipedia:Accuracy dispute">factual accuracy</a> may be compromised due to out-of-date information</b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please update this article to reflect recent events or newly available information.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">March 2019</span>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/South_American_Council_of_Health" title="South American Council of Health">South American Council of Health</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/South_American_Council_of_Health" title="South American Council of Health">South American Council of Health</a> is a UNASUR body established and approved on 16 December 2008, which brings together health ministers of the member states to develop regional programs in the region. Area of public health to be jointly financed by the South American bloc, to coordinate the energy policy of Unasur.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> It was created by decision of the Heads of State and Government of UNASUR, meeting extraordinarily in the Coast of Sauipe, <a href="/wiki/Bahia" title="Bahia">Bahia</a>, Brazil in December 2008. It was finally constituted on 21 April 2009 in <a href="/wiki/Santiago" title="Santiago">Santiago</a>, Chile.<sup id="cite_ref-G1_2008_52-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-G1_2008-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>It is a permanent council composed of Ministers from <a href="/wiki/UNASUR" class="mw-redirect" title="UNASUR">UNASUR</a> member countries. This body was created in order to constitute a space of integration concerning health, incorporating efforts and improvements from other mechanisms of regional integration, such as <a href="/wiki/MERCOSUR" class="mw-redirect" title="MERCOSUR">MERCOSUR</a>, ORAS CONHU and <a href="/wiki/ACTO" class="mw-redirect" title="ACTO">ACTO</a>, to promote common policies and coordinated activities among member countries. It is also a consultation and consensus body concerning health, which intends to delve deeply into relevant themes and strengthen public policies aimed at improving the living conditions of the inhabitants of the South American continent.
</p><p>Since health is an essential right to all human beings and all societies, and it is also a vital component for the development of mankind, the Health Council seeks political and social acceptance regarding the issue, proposing health to be seen as an important booster of cooperation and integration of the bloc's nations, intensifying the coordination of such nations and respecting diversity and interculturalism in the region.
</p><p>The Health Council aims to strengthen, by establishing a South American political institution with expertise in sanitary issues, the development of solutions to challenges that transcend national borders, developing values and mutual interests among the neighboring countries, thus facilitating the interaction of the Member States health authorities through the exchange of knowledge and technology in the region.
The South American Health Council (SHC) is composed of the Health Ministries of Unasur Member States. In order to achieve the Council's goals, the Coordinating Committee – responsible for preparing propositions of Agreements and Resolutions – was created. 
The Presidency of the Health Council is held by the Minister of Health of the country nominated for the Pro Tempore Presidency (PTP) of Unasur. It is in charge of coordinating the activities of all its bodies and managing the Technical Secretary. The Pro Tempore President has a two-year term that may be extended for another two years, being unconditionally succeeded by a president from a different country.
The SHC is supported by the Technical Secretary in charge of the Pro Tempore Presidency (PTP) and two countries of the previous and following PTP, in order to ensure the continuity of works. It is technically supported by the South American Institute for Government in Health (<a href="/wiki/South_American_Institute_of_Government_in_Health" title="South American Institute of Government in Health">ISAGS</a>). Additionally, it is composed of five Technical Groups 1- Health Surveillance and Response; 2- Development of Universal Health Systems; 3- Health Promotion and Action on Social Determinants; 4- Universal Access to Medicines; 5- Human Resources Development and Management) and six Structuring Networks (1- Network of National Institutes of Health (RINS); 2- Network of Health Technical Schools of UNASUR (RETS), 3- Network of National Institutions and Institutes of Cancer (RINC); 4- Network of Public Health Schools of Unasur (RESP); 5- Network of Disasters Risk Management; 6- Network of International Offices and International Cooperation in Health (REDSSUR-ORIS)<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/South_American_Institute_of_Government_in_Health" title="South American Institute of Government in Health">South American Institute of Government in Health</a> (ISAGS) of UNASUR is an intergovernmental entity of public character that has as main objective to promote the exchange, the critical reflection, the knowledge management and the generation of innovations in the field of Health policy and governance.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Summits">Summits</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Union_of_South_American_Nations&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Summits">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2010_Unasur_summit.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/2010_Unasur_summit.JPG/220px-2010_Unasur_summit.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/2010_Unasur_summit.JPG/330px-2010_Unasur_summit.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/2010_Unasur_summit.JPG/440px-2010_Unasur_summit.JPG 2x" data-file-width="5622" data-file-height="3748" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2010_Unasur_summit.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>South American leaders during the <a href="/wiki/2010_South_American_Summit" title="2010 South American Summit">Unasur 4th Summit</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Georgetown,_Guyana" title="Georgetown, Guyana">Georgetown</a>, Guyana.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Unasur_Lima_4.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Unasur_Lima_4.jpg/220px-Unasur_Lima_4.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Unasur_Lima_4.jpg/330px-Unasur_Lima_4.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Unasur_Lima_4.jpg/440px-Unasur_Lima_4.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2924" data-file-height="1940" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Unasur_Lima_4.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Heads of State at the <a href="/w/index.php?title=5th_UNASUR_Meeting&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="5th UNASUR Meeting (page does not exist)">5th UNASUR Meeting</a> in Lima, in Peru.</div></div></div>
<p>The first Union summit was held in Brasilia on 23 May 2008, in which the Constitutive Treaty was signed. Due to the political crisis that Bolivia faced, pro-tempore president Michelle Bachelet convened an emergency summit in Santiago, Chile, on 15 September 2008. The leaders of Argentina, Bolivia, Brazil and Brazil took part in this summit, in addition to President Michelle Bachelet, Colombia, Ecuador, Paraguay, Uruguay and Venezuela and the Secretary General of the OAS, José Miguel Insulza.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> After a six-hour meeting between the leaders in the Palacio de La Moneda, they finally declared their support for President Evo Morales's government and gave "its absolute support to Bolivia."<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<ul><li>An special UNASUR/<a href="/wiki/BRICS" title="BRICS">BRICS</a> leaders summit was held in <a href="/wiki/Fortaleza" title="Fortaleza">Fortaleza</a>, Brazil, in July 2014.</li>
<li>The 9th Summit, scheduled for April 23, 2016 in <a href="/wiki/Quito" title="Quito">Quito</a>, was canceled due to the <a href="/wiki/2016_Ecuador_earthquake" title="2016 Ecuador earthquake">Ecuador earthquake</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<p>There have been other presidential <i>extraordinary meetings</i>, such as:
</p>
<ul><li>May 2010: <a href="/wiki/Buenos_Aires" title="Buenos Aires">Buenos Aires</a>, Argentina. Election of Néstor Kirchner as <a href="/wiki/Secretary_General_of_UNASUR" class="mw-redirect" title="Secretary General of UNASUR">Secretary General</a>.</li>
<li>September 2010: Buenos Aires, Argentina. Discussion of the <a href="/wiki/2010_Ecuador_crisis" title="2010 Ecuador crisis">2010 Ecuador crisis</a>.</li>
<li>December 2010: <a href="/wiki/Mar_del_Plata" title="Mar del Plata">Mar del Plata</a>, Argentina. Kirchner's successor after his death. (Concurring with the 20th <a href="/wiki/Ibero-American_Summit" title="Ibero-American Summit">Ibero-American Summit</a>)</li>
<li>June 2012: <a href="/wiki/Mendoza,_Argentina" title="Mendoza, Argentina">Mendoza</a>, Argentina. Discussion on the <a href="/wiki/Impeachment_of_Fernando_Lugo" title="Impeachment of Fernando Lugo">Impeachment of Fernando Lugo</a> and suspension of Paraguay. (Concurring with the XLIII <a href="/wiki/Mercosur" title="Mercosur">Mercosur</a> presidential summit)</li>
<li>April 2013: Lima, Peru. Recognition of contested <a href="/wiki/2013_Venezuelan_presidential_election" title="2013 Venezuelan presidential election">Venezuelan presidential elections</a> results.<sup id="cite_ref-Maduro_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Maduro-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>July 2013: <a href="/wiki/Cochabamba" title="Cochabamba">Cochabamba</a>, Bolivia. Discussion on the <a href="/wiki/Evo_Morales" title="Evo Morales">Evo Morales</a> "kidnapping" incident in Europe (due to European/US suspicions that the Bolivian Presidential aircraft carried US fugitive <a href="/wiki/Edward_Snowden" title="Edward Snowden">Edward Snowden</a>.)</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Union_of_South_American_Nations&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="box-Update plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Update" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><img alt="Ambox current red.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/42px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png" decoding="async" width="42" height="34" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/63px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/84px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="360" data-file-height="290" /></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section's <b><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Accuracy_dispute" title="Wikipedia:Accuracy dispute">factual accuracy</a> may be compromised due to out-of-date information</b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please update this article to reflect recent events or newly available information.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">March 2019</span>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_South_America" title="Demographics of South America">Demographics of South America</a></div>
<p>At its peak of membership, UNASUR had a total population of 410 million inhabitants and a rate of population growth of about 0.6% per year. There were several different ecological regions such as <a href="/wiki/Tropical_forest" title="Tropical forest">tropical forests</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Atacama_Desert" title="Atacama Desert">Atacama Desert</a> and the icy portions of <a href="/wiki/Patagonia" title="Patagonia">Patagonia</a>. On the other hand, the continent presents regions of high population density, such as the great urban centers. The population is formed by descendants of Europeans (mainly <a href="/wiki/Spaniards" title="Spaniards">Spaniards</a>, Portuguese and Italians), <a href="/wiki/Africans" class="mw-redirect" title="Africans">Africans</a> and <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples" title="Indigenous peoples">indigenous</a>. There is a high percentage of <a href="/wiki/Mestizos" class="mw-redirect" title="Mestizos">mestizos</a> that vary greatly in composition according to each place. There is also a minor population of <a href="/wiki/Asians" class="mw-redirect" title="Asians">Asians</a>, especially in Brazil. The two main languages are by far Spanish and Portuguese, followed by French, English and Dutch in smaller numbers. Economically, Brazil, Argentina and Colombia are the wealthiest and most developed nations in the continent.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="Chile and Uruguay tend to do better in measures of human development and happiness; this needs clarification as well (February 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Union_of_South_American_Nations&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>, <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a> are the official languages of UNASUR. Spanish is the official language of Uruguay, Bolivia and Venezuela. <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a> is the official language of Suriname; English is the official language of Guyana.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Indigenous_languages_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous languages of the Americas">Indigenous languages</a> of UNASUR include <a href="/wiki/Wayuunaiki" class="mw-redirect" title="Wayuunaiki">Wayuunaiki</a> in northwestern Venezuela (<a href="/wiki/Zulia" title="Zulia">Zulia</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Guarani_language" title="Guarani language">Guaraní</a>,  <a href="/wiki/Quechua_languages" class="mw-redirect" title="Quechua languages">Quechua</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aymara_language" title="Aymara language">Aymara</a> in Bolivia. At least three South American indigenous languages (Quechua, Aymara, and Guarani) are recognized along with Spanish as national languages.
</p><p>Other languages found in UNASUR include, <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Hindustani" title="Caribbean Hindustani">Hindustani</a> and <a href="/wiki/Javanese_language" title="Javanese language">Javanese</a> in Suriname; Italian in Uruguay and Venezuela. Arabic speakers, often of <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_people" title="Lebanese people">Lebanese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Syrian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Syrian people">Syrian</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Palestinian people">Palestinian</a> descent, can be found in Arab communities in Venezuela.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Union_of_South_American_Nations&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>An estimated 87% of South Americans are Christians<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> (69% <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic">Roman Catholic</a>, 18% other Christian denominations mainly Traditional <a href="/wiki/Protestants" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestants">Protestants</a> and <a href="/wiki/Evangelicals" class="mw-redirect" title="Evangelicals">Evangelicals</a> but also <a href="/wiki/Orthodoxy" title="Orthodoxy">Orthodoxy</a>), accounting for ca. 19% of Christians worldwide.
</p><p>Due to the immigration of Indonesian workers, Suriname and Guyana have a large Hindu and Muslim community. Also <a href="/wiki/Kardecism" class="mw-redirect" title="Kardecism">Kardecist Spiritism</a> can be found in several countries along with <a href="/wiki/Afro-American_religion" title="Afro-American religion">Afro-American religions</a>. 
</p>

</td></tr>
